//\\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\\n364: // and error handling.\\n365: //\\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\\n368: \\tvar typ ItemType\\n369: \\n370: \\tif p.injecting {\\n371: \\t\\tp.injecting = false\\n372: \\t\\treturn int(p.inject)\\n373: \\t}\\n374: \\t// Skip comments.\\n375: \\tfor {\\n376: \\t\\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\\n377: \\t\\ttyp posrange.PositionRange{\\n386: \\t\\t\\tStart: p.lex.start,\\n387: \\t\\t\\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\\n388: \\t\\t}\\n389: \\t\\tp.addParseErr(pos, \\treturn int(typ)\\n401: }\\n402: \\n403: // Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\\n404: //\\n405: // It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\\n413: // This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\\n414: // https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\\n415: // Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\\n416: // Trying to inject when a previously injected Item has not yet been consumed will panic.\\n417: // Only Item types that are supposed to be used as start symbols are allowed as \\tp.injecting = true\\n429: }\\n430: \\n431: func (p *parser) newBinaryExpression(lhs Node, op Item, modifiers, rhs Node) *BinaryExpr {\\n432: \\tret := modifiers.(*BinaryExpr)\\n433: \\n434: Item is lexed that could be the end\n153: \t// of certain expressions its end position is stored here.\n154: \tlastClosing posrange.Pos\n155: \n156: \tyyParser yyParserImpl\n157: \n158: \tgeneratedParserResult any\n159: \tparseErrors           ParseErrors\n160: \n161: \t// lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet is set to true when the most recently\n162: \t// built histogram had a counter_reset_hint explicitly specified.\n163: \t// This is used to populate CounterResetHintSet in SequenceValue.\n164: \tlastHistogramCounterResetHintSet bool\n165: \n166: \toptions Options\n167: }\n168: \n169: // newParser returns a new low-level parser instance from the pool.\n170: func newParser(input string, opts Options) *parser {\n171: \tp := parserPool.Get().(*parser)\n172: \n173: \tp.functions = Functions\n174: \tp.injecting = false\n175: \tp.parseErrors = nil\n176: \tp.generatedParserResult = nil\n177: \tp.lastClosing = posrange.Pos(0)\n178: \tp.options = opts\n179: \n180: \t// Clear lexer struct before reusing.\n181: \tp.lex = Lexer{\n182: \t\tinput: input,\n183: \t\tstate: lexStatements,\n184: \t}\n185: \n186: \treturn p\n187: }\n188: \n189: // newParserWithFunctions opts)\n192: \tp.functions = functions\n193: \treturn p\n194: }\n195: \n196: func (p *parser) parseExpr() (expr Expr, err error) {\n197: \tdefer p.recover(&err)\n198: \n199: \tparseResult := p.parseGenerated(START_EXPRESSION)\n200: \n201: \tif parseResult != nil {\n202: \t\texpr = parseResult.(Expr)\n203: \t}\n204: \n205: \t// Only typecheck when there are no syntax errors.\n206: \tif func (p *parser) Close() {\n218: \tdefer parserPool.Put(p)\n219: }\n220: \n221: // ParseErr wraps a parsing error with line and position context.\n222: type ParseErr struct {\n223: \tPositionRange posrange.PositionRange\n224: \tErr           error\n225: \tQuery         string\n226: \n227: \t// LineOffset is an additional line offset to be added. Only used inside unit tests.\n228: \tLineOffset int\n229: }\n230: \n231: func (e *ParseErr) Error() string {\n232: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%s: parse error: %s\", e.PositionRange.StartPosInput(e.Query, e.LineOffset), e.Err)\n233: }\n234: \n235: type ParseErrors []ParseErr\n236: \n237: // Since producing multiple error messages might look weird when combined with error wrapping,\n238: // only the first error produced by the parser is included in the error string.\n239: // If getting the full error list is desired, it is recommended to typecast the error returned\n240: // by the parser to ParseErrors and work with the underlying slice.\n241: func (errs ParseErrors) Error() string {\n242: \tif len(errs) != 0 {\n243: \t\treturn errs[0].Error()\n244: \t}\n245: \t// Should never happen\n246: \t// Panicking while printing an error seems like a bad idea, so the\n247: \t// situation is explained in the error message instead.\n248: \treturn \"error contains no error message\"\n249: }\n250: \n251: // EnrichParseError enriches a single or list of parse errors (used for unit tests and promtool).\n252: func EnrichParseError(err error, enrich func(parseErr *ParseErr)) {\n253: \tvar parseErr *ParseErr\n254: \tif errors.As(err, &parseErr) {\n255: \t\tenrich(parseErr)\n256: \t}\n257: \tvar parseErrors ParseErrors\n258: \tif errors.As(err, &parseErrors) {\n259: \t\tfor i, e := range parseErrors {\n260: \t\t\tenrich(&e)\n261: \t\t\tparseErrors[i] = e\n262: \t\t}\n263: \t}\n264: }\n265: \n266: // SequenceValue is an omittable value in a sequence of time series values.\n267: type SequenceValue struct {\n268: \tValue     float64\n269: \tOmitted   bool\n270: \tHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n271: \t// CounterResetHintSet is true if the counter reset hint \"counter_reset_hint:unknown\" (verify it's unknown).\n275: \tCounterResetHintSet bool\n276: }\n277: \n278: func (v SequenceValue) String() string {\n279: \tif v.Omitted {\n280: \t\treturn \"_\"\n281: labels.Labels\n290: \tvalues []SequenceValue\n291: }\n292: \n293: // addParseErrf formats the error and appends it to the list of parsing errors.\n294: func (p *parser) addParseErrf(positionRange posrange.PositionRange, format string, args ...any) {\n295: \tp.addParseErr(positionRange, fmt.Errorf(format, args...))\n296: }\n297: \n298: // addParseErr appends the provided error to the list of parsing errors.\n299: func (p *parser) addParseErr(positionRange posrange.PositionRange, err error) {\n300: \tperr := ParseErr{\n301: \t\tPositionRange: positionRange,\n302: \t\tErr:           err,\n303: \t\tQuery:         p.lex.input,\n304: \t}\n305: \n306: \tp.parseErrors = append(p.parseErrors, perr)\n307: }\n308: \n309: func (p *parser) addSemanticError(err error) {\n310: \tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), err)\n311: }\n312: \n313: // unexpected creates a parser error complaining about an unexpected lexer item.\n314: // The item that is presented as unexpected is always the last item produced\n315: // by the lexer.\n316: func (p *parser) unexpected(context, expected string) {\n317: \tvar errMsg strings.Builder\n318: \n319: \t// Do not report lexer errors twice\n320: \tif p.yyParser.lval.item.Typ == ERROR {\n321: \t\treturn\n322: \t}\n323: \n324: \terrMsg.WriteString(\"unexpected \")\n325: \terrMsg.WriteString(p.yyParser.lval.item.desc())\n326: \n327: \tif context != \"\" {\n328: \t\terrMsg.WriteString(\" in \")\n329: \t\terrMsg.WriteString(context)\n330: \t}\n331: \n332: \tif expected != \"\" {\n333: \t\terrMsg.WriteString(\", expected \")\n334: \t\terrMsg.WriteString(expected)\n335: \t}\n336: \n337: \tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), errors.New(errMsg.String()))\n338: }\n339: \n340: var errUnexpected = errors.New(\"unexpected error\")\n341: \n342: // recover is the handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of Parse.\n343: func (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\n344: \te := recover()\n345: \tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\n346: \tcase ok:\n347: \t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n348: \t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n349: \t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n350: \n351: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"parser panic: %v\\n%s\", e, buf)\n352: \t\t*errp = errUnexpected\n353: \tcase e != nil:\n354: \t\t*errp = e.(error)\n355: \t}\n356: }\n357: \n358: // Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n359: // It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n360: // Comments are skipped.\n361: //\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n364: // and error handling.\n365: //\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n368: \tvar typ ItemType\n369: \n370: \tif p.injecting {\n371: \t\tp.injecting = false\n372: \t\treturn int(p.inject)\n373: \t}\n374: \t// Skip comments.\n375: \tfor {\n376: \t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n377: \t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n378: \t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n379: \t\t\tbreak\n380: \t\t}\n381: \t}\n382: \n383: \tswitch typ {\n384: \tcase ERROR:\n385: \t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n386: \t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n387: \t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n388: \t\t}\n389: \t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n390: \n391: \t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n392: \t\treturn 0\n393: \tcase EOF:\n394: \t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n395: \t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n396: \tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n397: \t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + posrange.Pos(len(lval.item.Val))\n398: \t}\n399: \n400: \treturn int(typ)\n401: }\n402: \n403: // Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n404: //\n405: // It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\n409: }\n410: \n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\n413: // This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n414: // https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n415: // Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n416: // Trying to inject when a previously injected Item has not yet been consumed will panic.\n417: // Only Item types that are supposed to be used as start symbols are allowed as an argument.\n418: func (p *parser) InjectItem(typ ItemType) {\n419: \tif p.injecting {\n420: \t\tpanic(\"cannot inject multiple Items into the token stream\")\n421: \t}\n422: \n423: \tif typ != 0 && (typ <= startSymbolsStart || typ >= startSymbolsEnd) {\n424: \t\tpanic(\"cannot inject symbol that isn't start symbol\")\n425: \t}\n426: \n427: \tp.inject = typ\n428: \tp.injecting = true\n429: }\n430: \n431: func (p *parser) {\n447: \t// If the metric name was set outside the braces, add a matcher for it.\n448: \t// If the metric name was inside the braces we don't need to do anything.\n449: \tif vs.Name != \"\" {\n450: \tret = modifier.(*AggregateExpr)\n460: \targuments := args.(Expressions)\n461: \n462: \tret.PosRange = posrange.PositionRange{\n463: \t\tStart: op.Pos,\n464: \t\tEnd:   p.lastClosing,\n465: \t}\n466: }\n499: \n500: // newMap is used when building the FloatHistogram from a map.\n501: func (*parser) newMap() (ret map[string]any) {\n502: \treturn map[string]any{}\n503: }\n504: \n505: // mergeMaps is provided AST. This includes type checking.\n720: func (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n721: \t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n722: \t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n723: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n724: \tcase Expressions:\n725: \t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n726: \tcase Expr:\n727: \t\ttyp = n.Type()\n728: \tdefault:\n729: \t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n730: \t}\n731: \n732: \t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n733: \t// errors in case of bad typing.\n734: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n735: \tcase *EvalStmt:\n736: \t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n737: \t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n738: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n739: \t\t}\n740: \n741: \tcase Expressions:\n742: \t\tfor _, e := range n {\n743: \t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n744: \t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n745: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n746: \t\t\t}\n747: \t\t}\n748: \tcase *AggregateExpr:\n749: \t\tif !n.Op.IsAggregator() {\n750: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"aggregation operator expected in aggregation expression but got %q\", n.Op)\n751: \t\t}\n752: \t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n753: \t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n754: \t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n757: \t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n758: \t\t}\n759: \n760: \tcase *BinaryExpr:\n761: \t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n762: \t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n763: \n764: \t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n765: \t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n766: \t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n767: \t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n768: \t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n769: \t\t\t}\n770: \t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n771: \t\t\t}\n772: \t\t\treturn r\n773: \t\t}\n774: \n775: \t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n776: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n777: \t\t}\n778: \n779: \t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n780: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n781: \t\t}\n782: \n783: \t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n784: \t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n785: \t\t}\n786: \n787: \t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n788: \t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n789: \t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n790: \t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n791: \t\t\t\t}\n792: \t\t\t}\n793: \t\t}\n794: \n795: \t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n796: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n797: \t\t}\n798: \t\tif lt != ValueTypeScalar && lt != ValueTypeVector {\n799: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.LHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n800: \t\t}\n801: \t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n802: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n803: \t\t}\n804: \n805: \t\tswitch {\n806: \t\tcase (lt != ValueTypeVector || rt != ValueTypeVector) && n.VectorMatching != nil:\n807: \t\t\tif len(n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels) > 0 {\n808: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector matching only allowed between instant vectors\")\n809: \t\t\t}\n810: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n811: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series only allowed between instant vectors\")\n812: \t\t\t}\n813: \t\t\tn.VectorMatching = nil\n814: \t\tcase n.Op.IsSetOperator(): // Both operands are Vectors.\n815: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToMany || n.VectorMatching.Card == CardManyToOne {\n816: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"no grouping allowed for %q operation\", n.Op)\n817: \t\t\t}\n818: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card != CardManyToMany {\n819: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operations must always be many-to-many\")\n820: \t\t\t}\n821: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n822: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series not allowed for set operators\")\n823: \t\t\t}\n824: \t\t}\n825: \n826: \t\tif (lt == ValueTypeScalar || rt == ValueTypeScalar) && n.Op.IsSetOperator() {\n827: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operator %q not allowed in binary scalar expression\", n.Op)\n828: \t\t}\n829: \n830: \tcase *Call:\n831: \t\tnargs := len(n.Func.ArgTypes)\n832: \t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n833: \t\t\tif nargs != len(n.Args) {\n834: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargs, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n835: \t\t\t}\n836: \t\t} else {\n837: \t\t\tna := nargs - 1\n838: \t\t\tif na > len(n.Args) {\n839: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at least %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", na, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n840: \t\t\t} else if nargsmax := na + n.Func.Variadic; n.Func.Variadic > 0 && nargsmax < len(n.Args) {\n841: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at most %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargsmax, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n842: \t\t\t}\n843: \t\t}\n844: \n845: \t\tif n.Func.Name == \"info\" && len(n.Args) > 1 {\n846: \t\t\t// Check the type is correct first\n847: \t\t\tif n.Args[1].Type() != ValueTypeVector {\n848: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(ValueTypeVector), fmt.Sprintf(\"call to function %q\", n.Func.Name), DocumentedType(n.Args[1].Type()))\n849: \t\t\t}\n850: \t\t\t// Check the vector selector in the len(n.Func.ArgTypes) {\n863: \t\t\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n864: \t\t\t\t\t// This is not a vararg function so we should not check the\n865: \t\t\t\t\t// type of the extra arguments.\n866: \t\t\t\t\tbreak\n867: \t\t\t\t}\n868: \t\t\t\ti = len(n.Func.ArgTypes) - 1\n869: \t\t\t}\n870: \t\t\tif t := p.checkAST(arg); t != n.Func.ArgTypes[i] {\n871: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(arg.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in call to function %q, got %s\", DocumentedType(n.Func.ArgTypes[i]), n.Func.Name, DocumentedType(t))\n872: \t\t\t}\n873: \t\t}\n874: allowed for unary expressions\")\n881: \t\t}\n882: \t\tif t := p.checkAST(n.Expr); t != ValueTypeScalar && t != ValueTypeVector {\n883: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unary expression only allowed on expressions of type scalar or instant vector, got %q\", DocumentedType(t))\n884: \t\t}\n885: \n886: \tcase *SubqueryExpr:\n887: \t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n888: \t\tif ty != check for non-empty matchers because an explicit\n906: \t\t\t// metric name is a non-empty matcher.\n907: \t\t\tbreak\n908: \t\t}\n909: \t\tif !n.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck {\n910: \t\t\t// A Vector \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher\")\n921: \t\t\t}\n922: \t\t}\n923: \n924: \tcase *NumberLiteral, *StringLiteral:\n925: \t\t// )\\n25: \\n26: // Node is a generic interface for all nodes in an AST.\\n27: //\\n28: // Whenever numerous nodes are listed such as in a switch-case statement\\n29: // or a chain of function The Visit method is\\n337: // invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\\n338: // If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\\n339: // of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\\n340: type Visitor interface {\\n341: \\tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\\n342: }\\n343: \\n344: // Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n345: // v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\\n346: // v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\\n347: // invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\\n348: // followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\\n349: // As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\\n350: func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\\n351: \\tvar err error\\n352: \\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\\n353: \\t\\treturn err\\n354: \\t}\\n355: \\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\\n356: \\n357: \\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\\n358: \\t\\tif pathToHere == nil {\\n359: \\t\\t\\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\\n360: \\t\\t}\\n361: \\t\\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\\n362: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n363: \\t\\t}\\n364: \\t}\\n365: \\n366: \\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\\n367: \\treturn err\\n368: }\\n369: \\n370: func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\\n371: \\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\\n372: \\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\\n373: \\t\\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\\n374: \\t\\tif ok {\\n375: \\t\\t\\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\\n376: \\t\\t}\\n377: \\t\\treturn nil\\n378: \\t})\\n379: \\treturn selectors\\n380: }\\n381: \\n382: type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\\n383: \\n384: func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\\n385: \\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\\n386: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n387: \\t}\\n388: \\n389: \\treturn f, nil\\n390: }\\n391: \\n392: // Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\\n393: // f(node, path); node must not be nil. Visitor allows visiting a Node and its child nodes. The Visit method is\n337: // invoked for each node with the path leading to the node provided additionally.\n338: // If the result visitor w is not nil and no error, Walk visits each of the children\n339: // of node with the visitor w, followed by a call of w.Visit(nil, nil).\n340: type Visitor interface {\n341: \tVisit(node Node, path []Node) (w Visitor, err error)\n342: }\n343: \n344: // Walk traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n345: // v.Visit(node, path); node must not be nil. If the visitor w returned by\n346: // v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\n347: // invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\n348: // followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\n349: // As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\n350: func Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\n351: \tvar err error\n352: \tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\n353: \t\treturn err\n354: \t}\n355: \tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\n356: \n357: \tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\n358: \t\tif pathToHere == nil {\n359: \t\t\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\n360: \t\t}\n361: \t\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\n362: \t\t\treturn err\n363: \t\t}\n364: \t}\n365: \n366: \t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\n367: \treturn err\n368: }\n369: \n370: func ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\n371: \tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\n372: \tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\n373: \t\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\n374: \t\tif ok {\n375: \t\t\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\n376: \t\t}\n377: \t\treturn nil\n378: \t})\n379: \treturn selectors\n380: }\n381: \n382: type inspector func(Node, []Node) error\n383: \n384: func (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\n385: \tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\n386: \t\treturn nil, err\n387: \t}\n388: \n389: \treturn f, nil\n390: }\n391: \n392: // Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n393: // f(node, path); node must not be nil. }\\n356: \\n357: // errorf returns an error token and terminates the scan by passing\\n358: // back a nil pointer that will be the next state, terminating l.NextItem.\\n359: func (l *Lexer) \\t}\\n388: \\treturn l\\n389: }\\n390: \\n391: // lineComment is the character that starts a line comment.\\n392: const lineComment = \\\"#\\\"\\n393: \\n394: // lexStatements is the top-level state r)\\n668: \\t}\\n669: }\\n670: \\n671: // lexInsideBraces scans the inside of a vector selector. {\\n679: \\tcase r == eof:\\n680: \\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unexpected end of input inside braces\\\")\\n681: \\tcase isSpace(r):\\n682: \\t\\treturn lexSpace\\n683: \\tcase isAlpha(r):\\n684: \\t\\tl.backup()\\n685: \\t\\treturn lexIdentifier\\n686: \\tcase r == ',':\\n687: \\t\\tl.emit(COMMA)\\n688: \\tcase r == '\\\"' || r == '\\\\'':\\n689: \\t\\tl.stringOpen = r\\n690: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n691: \\tcase r == '`':\\n692: \\t\\tl.stringOpen = r\\n693: \\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n694: \\tcase r == '=':\\n695: \\t\\tif l.next() == '~' {\\n696: \\t\\t\\tl.emit(EQL_REGEX)\\n697: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n698: \\t\\t}\\n699: \\t\\tl.backup()\\n700: \\t\\tl.emit(EQL)\\n701: \\tcase r == '!':\\n702: \\t\\tswitch nr := l.next(); {\\n732: \\tcase r == eof:\\n733: \\t\\treturn lexStatements\\n734: \\tcase r == '{' && l.peek() == '{':\\n735: \\t\\tif l.histogramState != histogramStateNone {\\n736: \\t\\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unexpected histogram opening {{\\\")\\n737: \\t\\t}\\n738: \\t\\tl.histogramState = histogramStateOpen\\n739: \\t\\tl.next()\\n740: \\t\\tl.emit(OPEN_HIST)\\n741: \\t\\treturn lexHistogram\\n742: \\tcase isSpace(r):\\n743: \\t\\tl.emit(SPACE)\\n744: \\t\\tlexSpace(l)\\n745: \\tcase r == '+':\\n746: \\t\\tl.emit(ADD)\\n747: \\tcase r == '-':\\n748: \\t\\tl.emit(SUB)\\n749: \\tcase r == 'x':\\n750: \\t\\tl.emit(TIMES)\\n751: \\tcase r == '_':\\n752: \\t\\tl.emit(BLANK)\\n753: \\tcase isDigit(r) || (r == '.' && isDigit(l.peek())):\\n754: \\t\\tl.backup()\\n755: \\t\\tlexNumber(l)\\n756: \\tcase isAlpha(r):\\n757: \\t\\tl.backup()\\n758: \\t\\t// We might lex invalid Items here but this will be caught by the parser.\\n759: \\t\\treturn lexKeywordOrIdentifier\\n760: \\tdefault:\\n761: \\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unexpected character in series sequence: %q\\\", r)\\n762: \\t}\\n763: \\treturn lexValueSequence\\n764: }\\n765: \\n766: // lexEscape scans a string escape sequence. The initial escaping character (\\\\)\\n767: // has already been seen.\\n768: //\\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \\\"go/scanner\\\"\\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n775: \\tvar n int\\n776: \\tvar base, maxVal uint32\\n777: \\n778: \\tch := l.next()\\n779: \\tswitch ch {\\n780: \\tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\\\\\', l.stringOpen:\\n781: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n782: \\tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\\n783: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\\n784: \\tcase 'x':\\n785: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n786: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\\n787: \\tcase 'u':\\n788: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n789: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n790: \\tcase 'U':\\n791: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n792: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n793: \\tcase eof:\\n794: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n795: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n796: \\tdefault:\\n797: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unknown escape sequence %#U\\\", ch)\\n798: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n799: \\t}\\n800: \\n801: \\tvar x uint32\\n802: \\tfor n > 0 {\\n803: \\t\\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\\n804: \\t\\tif d >= base {\\n805: \\t\\t\\tif ch == eof {\\n806: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n807: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n808: \\t\\t\\t}\\n809: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\\\", ch)\\n810: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n811: \\t\\t}\\n812: \\t\\tx = x*base + d\\n813: \\t\\tn--\\n814: \\n815: \\t\\t// Don't seek after last rune.\\n816: \\t\\tif n > 0 {\\n817: \\t\\t\\tch = l.next()\\n818: \\t\\t}\\n819: \\t}\\n820: \\n821: \\tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\\n822: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\\\")\\n823: \\t}\\n824: \\treturn lexString\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\\n828: // represent a valid digit.\\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\\n830: \\tswitch {\\n831: \\tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\\n832: \\t\\treturn int(ch - '0')\\n833: \\tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\\n834: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\\n835: \\tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\\n836: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\\n839: }\\n840: \\n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\\n843: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n844: \\t\\tl.next()\\n845: \\t}\\n846: \\tl.ignore()\\n847: }\\n848: \\n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n851: Loop:\\n852: \\tfor {\\n853: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n854: \\t\\tcase '\\\\\\\\':\\n855: \\t\\t\\treturn lexEscape\\n856: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n857: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n858: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n859: \\t\\tcase eof, '\\\\n':\\n860: \\t\\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unterminated quoted string\\\")\\n861: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n862: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n863: \\t\\t}\\n864: \\t}\\n865: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n866: \\treturn lexStatements\\n867: }\\n868: \\n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n871: Loop:\\n872: \\tfor {\\n873: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n874: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n875: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n876: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n877: \\t\\tcase eof:\\n878: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unterminated raw string\\\")\\n879: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n880: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n881: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n882: \\t\\t}\\n883: \\t}\\n884: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n885: \\treturn lexStatements\\n886: }\\n887: \\n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n890: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n891: \\t\\tl.next()\\n892: \\t}\\n893: \\tl.ignore()\\n894: \\treturn lexStatements\\n895: }\\n896: \\n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. This case is caught by the parser.\\n987: func (l *Lexer) scanNumber() bool {\\n988: \\tinitialPos := l.pos\\n989: \\t// Modify the digit pattern if the number is hexadecimal.\\n990: \\tdigitPattern \\t\\tl.emit(AT)\\n529: \\tdefault:\\n530: \\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unexpected character: %q\\\", r)\\n531: \\t}\\n532: \\treturn lexStatements\\n533: }\\n534: \\n535: func lexHistogram(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n536: \\tswitch l.histogramState {\\n537: \\tcase histogramStateMul:\\n538: \\t\\tl.histogramState = histogramStateNone\\n539: \\t\\tl.next()\\n540: \\t\\tl.emit(TIMES)\\n541: \\t\\treturn lexHistogramDescriptor(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n605: Loop:\\n606: \\tfor {\\n607: \\t\\tswitch r := l.next(); {\\n608: \\t\\tcase isAlpha(r):\\n609: \\t\\t\\t// absorb.\\n610: \\t\\tdefault:\\n611: \\t\\t\\tl.backup()\\n612: \\n613: \\t\\t\\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\\n614: \\t\\t\\tif desc, ok := histogramDesc[strings.ToLower(word)]; ok {\\n615: \\t\\t\\t\\tif l.peek() == ':' {\\n616: r)\\n668: \\t}\\n669: }\\n670: \\n671: // lexInsideBraces scans the inside of a vector selector. Keywords are ignored and\\n672: // scanned as identifiers.\\n673: func lexInsideBraces(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n674: \\tif strings.HasPrefix(l.input[l.pos:], lineComment) {\\n675: \\t\\treturn lexLineComment\\n676: \\t}\\n677: \\n678: \\tswitch r := l.next(); The initial escaping character (\\\\)\\n767: // has already been seen.\\n768: //\\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \\\"go/scanner\\\"\\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n775: \\tvar n int\\n776: \\tvar base, maxVal uint32\\n777: \\n778: \\tch := l.next()\\n779: \\tswitch ch {\\n780: \\tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\\\\\', l.stringOpen:\\n781: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n782: \\tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\\n783: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\\n784: \\tcase 'x':\\n785: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n786: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\\n787: \\tcase 'u':\\n788: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n789: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n790: \\tcase 'U':\\n791: \\t\\tch = l.next()\\n792: \\t\\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\\n793: \\tcase eof:\\n794: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n795: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n796: \\tdefault:\\n797: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unknown escape sequence %#U\\\", ch)\\n798: \\t\\treturn lexString\\n799: \\t}\\n800: \\n801: \\tvar x uint32\\n802: \\tfor n > 0 {\\n803: \\t\\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\\n804: \\t\\tif d >= base {\\n805: \\t\\t\\tif ch == eof {\\n806: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence not terminated\\\")\\n807: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n808: \\t\\t\\t}\\n809: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\\\", ch)\\n810: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n811: \\t\\t}\\n812: \\t\\tx = x*base + d\\n813: \\t\\tn--\\n814: \\n815: \\t\\t// Don't seek after last rune.\\n816: \\t\\tif n > 0 {\\n817: \\t\\t\\tch = l.next()\\n818: \\t\\t}\\n819: \\t}\\n820: \\n821: \\tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\\n822: \\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\\\")\\n823: \\t}\\n824: \\treturn lexString\\n825: }\\n826: \\n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\\n828: // represent a valid digit.\\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\\n830: \\tswitch {\\n831: \\tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\\n832: \\t\\treturn int(ch - '0')\\n833: \\tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\\n834: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\\n835: \\tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\\n836: \\t\\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\\n839: }\\n840: \\n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\\n843: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n844: \\t\\tl.next()\\n845: \\t}\\n846: \\tl.ignore()\\n847: }\\n848: \\n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n851: Loop:\\n852: \\tfor {\\n853: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n854: \\t\\tcase '\\\\\\\\':\\n855: \\t\\t\\treturn lexEscape\\n856: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n857: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n858: \\t\\t\\treturn lexString\\n859: \\t\\tcase eof, '\\\\n':\\n860: \\t\\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"unterminated quoted string\\\")\\n861: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n862: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n863: \\t\\t}\\n864: \\t}\\n865: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n866: \\treturn lexStatements\\n867: }\\n868: \\n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n871: Loop:\\n872: \\tfor {\\n873: \\t\\tswitch l.next() {\\n874: \\t\\tcase utf8.RuneError:\\n875: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"invalid UTF-8 rune\\\")\\n876: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n877: \\t\\tcase eof:\\n878: \\t\\t\\tl.errorf(\\\"unterminated raw string\\\")\\n879: \\t\\t\\treturn lexRawString\\n880: \\t\\tcase l.stringOpen:\\n881: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n882: \\t\\t}\\n883: \\t}\\n884: \\tl.emit(STRING)\\n885: \\treturn lexStatements\\n886: }\\n887: \\n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n890: \\tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\\n891: \\t\\tl.next()\\n892: \\t}\\n893: \\tl.ignore()\\n894: \\treturn lexStatements\\n895: }\\n896: \\n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. Left comment marker is known to be present.\\n898: func lexLineComment(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n899: \\tl.pos += posrange.Pos(len(lineComment))\\n900: \\tfor r := l.next(); !isEndOfLine(r) && r != eof; {\\n901: \\t\\tr = l.next()\\n902: \\t}\\n903: \\tl.backup()\\n904: \\tl.emit(COMMENT)\\n905: \\treturn lexStatements\\n906: }\\n907: \\n908: // lexNumber scans a number: decimal, hex, oct or float.\\n909: func lexNumber(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n910: \\tif !l.scanNumber() {\\n911: \\t\\treturn l.errorf(\\\"bad number syntax: %q\\\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\\n912: \\t}\\n913: \\tl.emit(NUMBER)\\n914: \\treturn lexStatements\\n915: }\\n916: \\n917: func (l *Lexer) scanDurationKeyword() bool {\\n918: \\tfor {\\n919: \\t\\tswitch r := l.next(); {\\n920: \\t\\tcase isAlpha(r):\\n921: \\t\\t\\t// absorb.\\n922: \\t\\tdefault:\\n923: \\t\\t\\tl.backup()\\n924: \\t\\t\\tword := l.input[l.start:l.pos]\\n925: \\t\\t\\tkw := strings.ToLower(word)\\n926: \\t\\t\\tswitch kw {\\n927: \\t\\t\\tcase \\\"step\\\":\\n928: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.emit(STEP)\\n929: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn true\\n930: \\t\\t\\tcase \\\"range\\\":\\n931: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.emit(RANGE)\\n932: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn true\\n933: \\t\\t\\tcase \\\"min\\\":\\n934: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.emit(MIN)\\n935: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn true\\n936: \\t\\t\\tcase \\\"max\\\":\\n937: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.emit(MAX)\\n938: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn true\\n939: \\t\\t\\tdefault:\\n940: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n941: \\t\\t\\t}\\n942: \\t\\t}\\n943: \\t}\\n944: }\\n945: \\n946: // lexNumberOrDuration scans a number or a duration Item.\\n947: func lexNumberOrDuration(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n948: \\tif l.scanNumber() {\\n949: \\t\\tl.emit(NUMBER)\\n950: \\t\\treturn lexStatements\\n951: \\t}\\n952: \\t// Next two chars must be a valid unit and a non-alphanumeric.\\n953: \\tif acceptRemainingDuration(l) {\\n954: \\t\\tl.backup()\\n955: \\t\\tl.emit(DURATION)\\n956: \\t\\treturn lexStatements\\n957: \\t}\\n958: \\treturn l.errorf(\\\"bad number or duration syntax: %q\\\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\\n959: }\\n960: \\n961: func acceptRemainingDuration(l *Lexer) bool {\\n962: \\t// Next two char must be a valid duration.\\n963: \\tif !l.accept(\\\"smhdwy\\\") {\\n964: \\t\\treturn false\\n965: \\t}\\n966: \\t// Support for ms. Bad units like hs, ys will be caught when we actually\\n967: \\t// parse the duration.\\n968: \\tl.accept(\\\"s\\\")\\n969: \\t// Next char can be another number then a unit.\\n970: \\tfor l.accept(\\\"0123456789\\\") {\\n971: \\t\\tfor l.accept(\\\"0123456789\\\") {\\n972: \\t\\t}\\n973: \\t\\t// y is no longer in the list as it should always come first in\\n974: \\t\\t// durations.\\n975: \\t\\tif !l.accept(\\\"smhdw\\\") {\\n976: \\t\\t\\treturn false\\n977: \\t\\t}\\n978: \\t\\t// Support for ms. Bad units like hs, ys will be caught when we actually\\n979: \\t\\t// parse the duration.\\n980: \\t\\tl.accept(\\\"s\\\")\\n981: \\t}\\n982: \\treturn !isAlphaNumeric(l.next())\\n983: }\\n984: \\n985: // scanNumber scans numbers of different formats. The scanned Item is\\n986: // not necessarily a valid number. This case is caught by the parser.\\n987: func (l *Lexer) scanNumber() bool {\\n988: \\tinitialPos := l.pos\\n989: \\t// Modify the digit pattern if the number is hexadecimal.\\n990: \\tdigitPattern := \\\"0123456789\\\"\\n991: \\t// Disallow hexadecimal in series descriptions as the syntax is ambiguous.\\n992: \\tif !l.seriesDesc &&\\n993: \\t\\tl.accept(\\\"0\\\") && l.accept(\\\"xX\\\") {\\n994: \\t\\tl.accept(\\\"_\\\") // eg., 0X_1FFFP-16 == 0.1249847412109375\\n995: \\t\\tdigitPattern = \\\"0123456789abcdefABCDEF\\\"\\n996: \\t}\\n997: \\tconst (\\n998: \\t\\t// Define dot, exponent, and underscore patterns.\\n999: \\t\\tdotPattern        = \\\".\\\"\\n1000: \\t\\texponentPattern   = \\\"eE\\\"\\n1001: \\t\\tunderscorePattern = \\\"_\\\"\\n1002: \\t\\t// Anti-patterns are rune sets that cannot follow their respective rune.\\n1003: \\t\\tdotAntiPattern        = \\\"_.\\\"\\n1004: \\t\\texponentAntiPattern   = \\\"._eE\\\" // and EOL.\\n1005: \\t\\tunderscoreAntiPattern = \\\"._eE\\\" // and EOL.\\n1006: \\t)\\n1007: \\t// All numbers follow the prefix: [.][d][d._eE]*\\n1008: \\tl.accept(dotPattern)\\n1009: \\tl.accept(digitPattern)\\n1010: \\t// [d._eE]* hereon.\\n1011: \\tdotConsumed := false\\n1012: \\texponentConsumed := false\\n1013: \\tfor l.is(digitPattern + dotPattern + underscorePattern + exponentPattern) {\\n1014: \\t\\t// \\\".\\\" cannot repeat.\\n1015: \\t\\tif l.is(dotPattern) {\\n1016: \\t\\t\\tif dotConsumed {\\n1017: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.accept(dotPattern)\\n1018: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n1019: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1020: \\t\\t}\\n1021: \\t\\t// \\\"eE\\\" cannot repeat.\\n1022: \\t\\tif l.is(exponentPattern) {\\n1023: \\t\\t\\tif exponentConsumed {\\n1024: \\t\\t\\t\\tl.accept(exponentPattern)\\n1025: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n1026: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1027: \\t\\t}\\n1028: \\t\\t// Handle dots.\\n1029: \\t\\tif l.accept(dotPattern) {\\n1030: \\t\\t\\tdotConsumed = true\\n1031: \\t\\t\\tif l.accept(dotAntiPattern) {\\n1032: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n1033: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1034: \\t\\t\\t// Fractional hexadecimal literals are not allowed.\\n1035: \\t\\t\\tif len(digitPattern) > 10 /* 0x[\\\\da-fA-F].[\\\\d]+p[\\\\d] */ {\\n1036: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n1037: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1038: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n1039: \\t\\t}\\n1040: \\t\\t// Handle exponents.\\n1041: \\t\\tif l.accept(exponentPattern) {\\n1042: \\t\\t\\texponentConsumed = true\\n1043: \\t\\t\\tl.accept(\\\"+-\\\")\\n1044: \\t\\t\\tif l.accept(exponentAntiPattern) || l.peek() == eof {\\n1045: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n1046: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1047: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n1048: \\t\\t}\\n1049: \\t\\t// Handle underscores.\\n1050: \\t\\tif l.accept(underscorePattern) {\\n1051: \\t\\t\\tif l.accept(underscoreAntiPattern) || l.peek() == eof {\\n1052: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn false\\n1053: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1054: \\n1055: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n1056: \\t\\t}\\n1057: \\t\\t// Handle digits at the end since we already consumed before this loop.\\n1058: \\t\\tl.acceptRun(digitPattern)\\n1059: \\t}\\n1060: \\t// Empty string is not a valid number.\\n1061: \\tif l.pos == initialPos {\\n1062: \\t\\treturn false\\n1063: \\t}\\n1064: \\t// Next thing must not be alphanumeric unless it's the times token\\n1065: \\t// for series repetitions.\\n1066: \\tif r := l.peek(); The next character\\n1073: // is known to be a letter.\\n1074: func lexIdentifier(l *Lexer) stateFn {\\n1075: \\tfor isAlphaNumeric(l.next()) {\\n1076: \\t\\t// absorb\\n1077: \\t}\\n1078: \\tl.backup()\\n1079: \\tl.emit(IDENTIFIER)\\n1080: \\treturn lexStatements\\n1081: }\\n1082: \\n1083: // lexKeywordOrIdentifier scans an alphanumeric identifier which may contain\\n1084: // a colon rune. Keywords are ignored and\n672: // scanned as identifiers.\n673: func lexInsideBraces(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n674: \tif strings.HasPrefix(l.input[l.pos:], lineComment) {\n675: \t\treturn lexLineComment\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tswitch r := l.next(); The initial escaping character (\\)\n767: // has already been seen.\n768: //\n769: // NOTE: This function as well as the helper function digitVal() and associated\n770: // tests have been adapted from the corresponding functions in the \"go/scanner\"\n771: // package of the Go standard library to work for Prometheus-style strings.\n772: // None of the actual escaping/quoting logic was changed in this function - it\n773: // was only modified to integrate with our lexer.\n774: func lexEscape(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n775: \tvar n int\n776: \tvar base, maxVal uint32\n777: \n778: \tch := l.next()\n779: \tswitch ch {\n780: \tcase 'a', 'b', 'f', 'n', 'r', 't', 'v', '\\\\', l.stringOpen:\n781: \t\treturn lexString\n782: \tcase '0', '1', '2', '3', '4', '5', '6', '7':\n783: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 3, 8, 255\n784: \tcase 'x':\n785: \t\tch = l.next()\n786: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 2, 16, 255\n787: \tcase 'u':\n788: \t\tch = l.next()\n789: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 4, 16, unicode.MaxRune\n790: \tcase 'U':\n791: \t\tch = l.next()\n792: \t\tn, base, maxVal = 8, 16, unicode.MaxRune\n793: \tcase eof:\n794: \t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence not terminated\")\n795: \t\treturn lexString\n796: \tdefault:\n797: \t\tl.errorf(\"unknown escape sequence %#U\", ch)\n798: \t\treturn lexString\n799: \t}\n800: \n801: \tvar x uint32\n802: \tfor n > 0 {\n803: \t\td := uint32(digitVal(ch))\n804: \t\tif d >= base {\n805: \t\t\tif ch == eof {\n806: \t\t\t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence not terminated\")\n807: \t\t\t\treturn lexString\n808: \t\t\t}\n809: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"illegal character %#U in escape sequence\", ch)\n810: \t\t\treturn lexString\n811: \t\t}\n812: \t\tx = x*base + d\n813: \t\tn--\n814: \n815: \t\t// Don't seek after last rune.\n816: \t\tif n > 0 {\n817: \t\t\tch = l.next()\n818: \t\t}\n819: \t}\n820: \n821: \tif x > maxVal || 0xD800 <= x && x < 0xE000 {\n822: \t\tl.errorf(\"escape sequence is an invalid Unicode code point\")\n823: \t}\n824: \treturn lexString\n825: }\n826: \n827: // digitVal returns the digit value of a rune or 16 in case the rune does not\n828: // represent a valid digit.\n829: func digitVal(ch rune) int {\n830: \tswitch {\n831: \tcase '0' <= ch && ch <= '9':\n832: \t\treturn int(ch - '0')\n833: \tcase 'a' <= ch && ch <= 'f':\n834: \t\treturn int(ch - 'a' + 10)\n835: \tcase 'A' <= ch && ch <= 'F':\n836: \t\treturn int(ch - 'A' + 10)\n837: \t}\n838: \treturn 16 // Larger than any legal digit val.\n839: }\n840: \n841: // skipSpaces skips the spaces until a non-space is encountered.\n842: func skipSpaces(l *Lexer) {\n843: \tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\n844: \t\tl.next()\n845: \t}\n846: \tl.ignore()\n847: }\n848: \n849: // lexString scans a quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\n850: func lexString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n851: Loop:\n852: \tfor {\n853: \t\tswitch l.next() {\n854: \t\tcase '\\\\':\n855: \t\t\treturn lexEscape\n856: \t\tcase utf8.RuneError:\n857: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"invalid UTF-8 rune\")\n858: \t\t\treturn lexString\n859: \t\tcase eof, '\\n':\n860: \t\t\treturn l.errorf(\"unterminated quoted string\")\n861: \t\tcase l.stringOpen:\n862: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n863: \t\t}\n864: \t}\n865: \tl.emit(STRING)\n866: \treturn lexStatements\n867: }\n868: \n869: // lexRawString scans a raw quoted string. The initial quote has already been seen.\n870: func lexRawString(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n871: Loop:\n872: \tfor {\n873: \t\tswitch l.next() {\n874: \t\tcase utf8.RuneError:\n875: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"invalid UTF-8 rune\")\n876: \t\t\treturn lexRawString\n877: \t\tcase eof:\n878: \t\t\tl.errorf(\"unterminated raw string\")\n879: \t\t\treturn lexRawString\n880: \t\tcase l.stringOpen:\n881: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n882: \t\t}\n883: \t}\n884: \tl.emit(STRING)\n885: \treturn lexStatements\n886: }\n887: \n888: // lexSpace scans a run of space characters. One space has already been seen.\n889: func lexSpace(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n890: \tfor isSpace(l.peek()) {\n891: \t\tl.next()\n892: \t}\n893: \tl.ignore()\n894: \treturn lexStatements\n895: }\n896: \n897: // lexLineComment scans a line comment. Left comment marker is known to be present.\n898: func lexLineComment(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n899: \tl.pos += posrange.Pos(len(lineComment))\n900: \tfor r := l.next(); !isEndOfLine(r) && r != eof; {\n901: \t\tr = l.next()\n902: \t}\n903: \tl.backup()\n904: \tl.emit(COMMENT)\n905: \treturn lexStatements\n906: }\n907: \n908: // lexNumber scans a number: decimal, hex, oct or float.\n909: func lexNumber(l *Lexer) stateFn {\n910: \tif !l.scanNumber() {\n911: \t\treturn l.errorf(\"bad number syntax: %q\", l.input[l.start:l.pos])\n912: \t}\n913: \tl.emit(NUMBER)\n914: \treturn lexStatements\n915: }\n916: \n917: func (l *Lexer) scanDurationKeyword() bool {\n918: \tfor {\n919: \t\tswitch r := l.next(); query parsing and validation pipeline in prometheus/prometheus is implemented through several key components:\\n\\n## Parser Interface and Implementation\\n\\n**promql/parser/parse.go** contains the main Parser interface and implementations:\\n- `Parser` (interface) - defines the public API with methods like `ParseExpr(input string) (Expr, error)`, `ParseMetric()`, `ParseMetricSelector()`, etc.\\n- `promQLParser` (struct) - implements the Parser interface\\n- `parser` (struct) - low-level parser used internally that manages lexer, yacc parser, and function registry\\n- `ParseExpr()` method - entry point for parsing expressions, calls `parseGenerated()` and then `checkAST()` for validation\\n- `checkAST()` method - performs semantic validation and type checking of the AST, handling various node types and enforcing type constraints\\n- `NewParser()` function - creates parser instances with configurable Options\\n\\n## AST Node Type Definitions\\n\\n**promql/parser/ast.go** defines all expression and statement node types:\\n- `Node` (interface) - generic interface for all AST nodes\\n- `Expr` (interface) - generic interface for all expression types\\n- `Statement` (interface) - generic interface for all statement types\\n- Expression types (alphabetically): `AggregateExpr`, `BinaryExpr`, `Call`, `DurationExpr`, `MatrixSelector`, `NumberLiteral`, `ParenExpr`, `StringLiteral`, `SubqueryExpr`, `UnaryExpr`, `VectorSelector`, `StepInvariantExpr`\\n- Statement types: `EvalStmt`, `TestStmt`\\n- Vector matching: `VectorMatching`, `VectorMatchCardinality`, `VectorMatchFillValues`\\n- Position tracking: integration with posrange for error reporting\\n\\n## Lexer Tokenizer\\n\\n**promql/parser/lex.go** implements the lexical analyzer:\\n- `Lexer` (struct) - tokenizes input strings with state management for different parsing contexts\\n- `Item` (struct) - represents a token with Type, Position, and Value\\n- `ItemType` (const int) - enumeration of token types including operators, keywords, aggregators, literals, etc.\\n- `NextItem()` method - produces the next token from input\\n- `Lex()` function - creates a new Lexer instance\\n- Lexing functions: `lexStatements()`, `lexInsideBraces()`, `lexKeywordOrIdentifier()`, `lexNumber()`, `lexString()`, `lexIdentifier()`, etc.\\n- Token categories: operators (ADD, SUB, MUL, DIV, POW, etc.), comparison operators (EQLC, NEQ, LTE, LSS, GTE, GTR), aggregators (SUM, AVG, COUNT, MAX, MIN, TOPK, BOTTOMK, etc.), keywords (ON, BY, GROUP_LEFT, GROUP_RIGHT, BOOL, OFFSET, etc.)\\n\\n## Generated Yacc Parser\\n\\n**promql/parser/generated_parser.y** - YACC grammar definition file that specifies:\\n- Grammar rules for expressions, statements, and metric selectors\\n- Multiple start symbols (START_EXPRESSION, START_METRIC, START_METRIC_SELECTOR, START_SERIES_DESCRIPTION)\\n- Token definitions and their union types\\n- Operator precedence and associativity\\n- Actions that construct AST nodes\\n\\n**promql/parser/generated_parser.y.go** - Generated parser implementation from goyacc:\\n- Contains the actual parser state machine and parsing logic\\n- Implements `yyParser` interface\\n- Integrates with Lexer through the yyLexer interface\\n- Defines all ItemType constants as numeric values\\n- Produces parse results that are AST nodes\\n\\n## Function Registry\\n\\n**promql/parser/functions.go** defines valid PromQL functions:\\n- `Function` (struct) - represents a function with Name, ArgTypes (slice of ValueType), Variadic flag, ReturnType, and Experimental flag\\n- `Functions` (map) - global registry of all ~90+ supported functions including:\\n  - Range vector functions: rate, irate, increase, delta, deriv, changes, etc.\\n  - Instant vector functions: abs, ceil, floor, sqrt, exp, ln, log2, log10, etc.\\n  - Aggregation functions: sum, avg, count, min, max, group, stddev, stdvar, topk, bottomk, etc.\\n  - Time/date functions: time, hour, minute, month, day_of_week, day_of_month, day_of_year, days_in_month, year\\n  - Math functions: sin, cos, tan, asin, acos, atan, sinh, cosh, tanh, deg, rad, sgn\\n  - Histogram functions: histogram_quantile, histogram_sum, histogram_count, histogram_avg, etc.\\n  - Utility functions: scalar, vector, label_join, label_replace, etc.\\n- `getFunction()` - retrieves a function from the registry\\n\\n## Value Type System\\n\\n**promql/parser/value.go** defines expression type validation:\\n- `ValueType` (string constants) - enumeration of possible expression types:\\n  - ValueTypeNone - invalid or no type\\n  - ValueTypeScalar - scalar values\\n  - ValueTypeVector - instant vectors\\n  - ValueTypeMatrix - range vectors\\n  - ValueTypeString - string literals\\n- `Value` (interface) - generic interface for evaluated values\\n- `DocumentedType()` function - converts internal types to user-facing documentation strings\\n\\n## Position Tracking\\n\\n**promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go** provides position range tracking:\\n- `Pos` (int) - represents a position in the input string\\n- `PositionRange` (struct) - represents a range [Start, End] for error reporting\\n- `StartPosInput()` method - converts position range to human-readable line:column format\\n\\n## Query Execution Engine\\n\\n**promql/engine.go** integrates the parser into the execution pipeline:\\n- `Engine` (struct) - orchestrates query parsing and evaluation\\n- `NewEngine()` - creates engine instances\\n- `Eval()` - parses expressions using the Parser and evaluates them\\n- Imports and uses parser types for query preparation and execution\\n\\n**promql/functions.go** implements the actual function evaluation logic:\\n- `FunctionCall` (type) - function signature for all function implementations\\n- ~100+ function implementations (funcTime, funcRate, funcAbsent, etc.)\\n- Integration with the parser's Function registry\\n\\n## Complete Parsing Pipeline\\n\\nThe pipeline flow is:\\n1. Input string → Lexer (promql/parser/lex.go) tokenizes into Items\\n2. Token stream → Generated Parser (promql/parser/generated_parser.y.go) parses using YACC grammar\\n3. Parser actions construct AST nodes (promql/parser/ast.go)\\n4. AST → checkAST() (promql/parser/parse.go) validates:\\n   - Type checking using Function registry and ValueType system\\n   - Semantic constraints on operators, aggregators, and matchers\\n   - Vector matching rules and cardinality constraints\\n5. Validated AST → Engine (promql/engine.go) for execution\\n6. Engine evaluates using function implementations (promql/functions.go)\\n\\nAll components are tightly integrated with position tracking (posrange) for precise error reporting that includes line and column information for debugging invalid queries.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4760,"cache_read_input_tokens":97339,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4760},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"9deef6e0-5ebe-4c46-bd52-903c491d6a51","uuid":"e6dc779a-89d1-4f66-9b2a-e123391125b9"}

GROUP_RIGHT, BOOL, OFFSET, etc.)\\n\\n## Generated Yacc Parser\\n\\n**promql/parser/generated_parser.y** - YACC grammar definition file that specifies:\\n- Grammar rules for expressions, statements, and metric selectors\\n- Multiple start symbols (START_EXPRESSION, START_METRIC, START_METRIC_SELECTOR, START_SERIES_DESCRIPTION)\\n- Token definitions and their union types\\n- Operator precedence and associativity\\n- Actions that construct AST nodes\\n\\n**promql/parser/generated_parser.y.go** - Generated parser implementation from goyacc:\\n- Contains the actual parser state machine and parsing logic\\n- Implements `yyParser` interface\\n- Integrates with Lexer through the yyLexer interface\\n- Defines all ItemType constants as numeric values\\n- Produces parse results that are AST nodes\\n\\n## Function Registry\\n\\n**promql/parser/functions.go** defines valid PromQL functions:\\n- `Function` (struct) - represents a function with Name, ArgTypes (slice of ValueType), Variadic flag, ReturnType, and Experimental flag\\n- `Functions` (map) - global registry of all ~90+ supported functions including:\\n  - Range vector functions: rate, irate, increase, delta, deriv, changes, etc.\\n  - Instant vector functions: abs, ceil, floor, sqrt, exp, ln, log2, log10, etc.\\n  - Aggregation functions: sum, avg, count, min, max, group, stddev, stdvar, topk, bottomk, etc.\\n  - Time/date functions: time, hour, minute, month, day_of_week, day_of_month, day_of_year, days_in_month, year\\n  - Math functions: sin, cos, tan, asin, acos, atan, sinh, cosh, tanh, deg, rad, sgn\\n  - Histogram functions: histogram_quantile, histogram_sum, histogram_count, histogram_avg, etc.\\n  - Utility functions: scalar, vector, label_join, label_replace, etc.\\n- `getFunction()` - retrieves a function from the registry\\n\\n## Value Type System\\n\\n**promql/parser/value.go** defines expression type validation:\\n- `ValueType` (string constants) - enumeration of possible expression types:\\n  - ValueTypeNone - invalid or no type\\n  - ValueTypeScalar - scalar values\\n  - ValueTypeVector - instant vectors\\n  - ValueTypeMatrix - range vectors\\n  - ValueTypeString - string literals\\n- `Value` (interface) - generic interface for evaluated values\\n- `DocumentedType()` function - converts internal types to user-facing documentation strings\\n\\n## Position Tracking\\n\\n**promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go** provides position range tracking:\\n- `Pos` (int) - represents a position in the input string\\n- `PositionRange` (struct) - represents a range [Start, End] for error reporting\\n- `StartPosInput()` method - converts position range to human-readable line:column format\\n\\n## Query Execution Engine\\n\\n**promql/engine.go** integrates the parser into the execution pipeline:\\n- `Engine` (struct) - orchestrates query parsing and evaluation\\n- `NewEngine()` - creates engine instances\\n- `Eval()` - parses expressions using the Parser and evaluates them\\n- Imports and uses parser types for query preparation and execution\\n\\n**promql/functions.go** implements the actual function evaluation logic:\\n- `FunctionCall` (type) - function signature for all function implementations\\n- ~100+ function implementations (funcTime, funcRate, funcAbsent, etc.)\\n- Integration with the parser's Function registry\\n\\n## Complete Parsing Pipeline\\n\\nThe pipeline flow is:\\n1. Input string → Lexer (promql/parser/lex.go) tokenizes into Items\\n2. Token stream → Generated Parser (promql/parser/generated_parser.y.go) parses using YACC grammar\\n3. Parser actions construct AST nodes (promql/parser/ast.go)\\n4. AST → checkAST() (promql/parser/parse.go) validates:\\n   - Type checking using Function registry and ValueType system\\n   - Semantic constraints on operators, aggregators, and matchers\\n   - Vector matching rules and cardinality constraints\\n5. Validated AST → Engine (promql/engine.go) for execution\\n6. Engine evaluates using function implementations (promql/functions.go)\\n\\nAll components are tightly integrated with position tracking (posrange) for precise error reporting that includes line and column information for debugging invalid queries.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
